                     </table>
               </div>
               
               
               
               <div class="article-section__table-footnotes">
                  <ul>
                     <li id="adfm202411280-tbl2-note-0001">1C ≈ 129&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.</li>
                  </ul>
               </div>
               <div class="article-section__table-source"></div>
            </div>
            
            <p>Similar to Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, the modification means of NFPP are mainly classified as follows: unit cell modification by doping (Mn doping, Ti doping, anion doping, etc.), carbon coating, and morphology modification.</p>
            
            <p>Among the research on carbon coating methods, the NFPP/C material synthesized by Ren et&nbsp;al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0056_R_d9736424e3295" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Energy Storage Mater.">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> via the electrospinning technique is particularly outstanding in terms of electrochemical performance, with a first-cycle specific capacity of up to 137.2 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, even higher than its theoretical specific capacity of 129.0 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0009">9a</a>). Later it was illustrated that the extra capacity originated from the 3D carbon network. The NFPP/C nanofibre electrodes also exhibited excellent rate performance (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0009">9b,c</a>). Reversible capacities of 136, 118, 112, 105, 94, 85, 78, and 64 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> were achieved at rates of 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, 10, and 20&nbsp;C, respectively. When the current rate was tuned back to 0.1&nbsp;C again, the reversible capacity could be fully recovered. In the full cell combined with hard carbon (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0009">9d</a>), the initial two charge/discharge profiles under a voltage window of 1.7–4.3&nbsp;V are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0009">9e</a>. NFPP/C//HC full cell delivers a reversible capacity of 126.4 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with an average discharge voltage of 2.9&nbsp;V at a current rate of 20&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Pouch cells were also assembled with NFPP/C nanofibers, which exhibited a capacity of 86.7 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at the current density of 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0009">9f</a>).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202411280-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e6a53f9e-1887-43f3-9177-73864bcb2835/adfm202411280-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/e6a53f9e-1887-43f3-9177-73864bcb2835/adfm202411280-fig-0009-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/359011bd-ec74-4071-ac79-ad9369576688/adfm202411280-fig-0009-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e6a53f9e-1887-43f3-9177-73864bcb2835/adfm202411280-fig-0009-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 9<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202411280-fig-0009&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202411280" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a–f) Studies of NFPP/C nanofibre cathode. (a) GCD profile at 0.1&nbsp;C, b,c) Charge–discharge curves of NFPP/C nanofibre at different current densities, d) Schematic illustration of the NFPP/C//HC full cell, and e) initial charge–discharge curve of the full cell at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. (f) GCD profile of a pouch cell. g–i) Studies of NFPP@MCNTs cathode. a–f) Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0056" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0056_R_d9736424e3357" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Energy Storage Mater.">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2023, Elsevier B.V. g) The CV curves of NFPP@MCNTs at 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. h) The initial charge/discharge curves of NFPP@MCNTs at 10&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, (i) the specific capacity and corresponding Coulombic efficiency of 1200th cycle number at 2&nbsp;C. g–i) Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0067" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0067_R_d9736424e3367" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - J. Power Sources">67</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2020, Elsevier B.V.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>In the study of Cao,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0067" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0067_R_d9736424e3375" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - J. Power Sources">67</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> NFPP was prepared by a simple spray-drying method followed by multi-layer carbon nanotube capping, and the electrochemical performance of the obtained NFPP@MCNTs is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0009">9g–i</a>. The CV curves at 0.05&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> exhibited six pairs of redox peaks at 2.47/2.51&nbsp;V, 2.84/2.98&nbsp;V, 3.02/3.09&nbsp;V, 3.08/3.15&nbsp;V, 3.14/3.21&nbsp;V, and 3.17/3.25&nbsp;V, respectively. These potential values are very close to the equilibrium potentials of the Fe<sup>3+</sup>/Fe<sup>2+</sup> redox pairs in NFPP, and the overlap of the two cycles indicates excellent reversibility. In the redox process, the redox peaks at 2.47/2.51&nbsp;V and 2.84/2.98&nbsp;V correspond to the oxidation of NFPP to Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub> process. And the redox peaks at 3.02/3.09&nbsp;V, 3.08/3.15&nbsp;V, 3.14/3.21&nbsp;V, and 3.17/3.25&nbsp;V correspond to the electrochemical reduction process of Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub> to NaFe<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0009">9h</a> shows the initial charge/discharge curve of NFPP@MCNTs at 0.1&nbsp;C. The initial charging capacity was as high as 115.7 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which reached 89.6% of the theoretical capacity and had a Coulombic efficiency of 99.7%. The reversible specific capacity can be up to 96.7 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and reserves 92.8 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2 C after 1200 cycles with the corresponding Coulombic efficiency of &gt;99% during all of the cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0009">9i</a>).</p>
            
            <p>In addition, high-entropy doping of multiple cation combinations has attracted much attention in the modulation of crystal structure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0071_R_d9736424e3442" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 71 - Small">71</a>, <a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0072" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0072_R_d9736424e3442" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 72 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">72</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Li et&nbsp;al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0073" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0073_R_d9736424e3447" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 73 - Small Methods">73</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> proposed an entropy-enhanced Na<sub>4</sub>Fe<sub>2.95</sub>(NiCoMnMgZn)<sub>0.01</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub> (HE-NFPP) cathode with excellent rate performance (67.1 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 50C rate) and cycling performance (92.0% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 1 C). The sodium storage mechanism of HE-NFPP, i.e., incomplete solid solution reaction driven by Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup> redox electric pair, was shown using in situ XRD with a volume change of only 4.0%. The structural distortion and sudden rearrangement were effectively suppressed by high entropy doping. A punch cell with the HE-NFPP cathode and hard carbon anode was also fabricated. As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0010">10a,b</a>, the full cell displayed an average operating voltage of 3.0&nbsp;V, a maximum energy density of 165&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> (based on the total mass of active materials), and their Coulombic efficiency could be stabilized at &gt;99.5% with the increase of the number of cycles.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202411280-fig-0010"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/98f69f04-7f0e-4559-930c-88f11492fbd4/adfm202411280-fig-0010-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/98f69f04-7f0e-4559-930c-88f11492fbd4/adfm202411280-fig-0010-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/09136d64-cf12-4844-a6cb-804feb5f44bc/adfm202411280-fig-0010-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/98f69f04-7f0e-4559-930c-88f11492fbd4/adfm202411280-fig-0010-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 10<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202411280-fig-0010&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202411280" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Study of HC||HE-NFPP full cell. a) Schematic diagram of the HC||HE-NFPP full cell. b) The first three cycles of the pouch cell at 0.1&nbsp;C (cathode: 242.3&nbsp;mg; anode: 89.4&nbsp;mg). a,b) Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0073" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0073_R_d9736424e3502" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 73 - Small Methods">73</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2024, Wiley-VCH. The cycling performance of c) 5&nbsp;C and d) 10&nbsp;C rate at 60&nbsp;°C. c,d) Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0075" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0075_R_d9736424e3507" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 75 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">75</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2023, American Chemical Society. e)The cycling performance of NFPP and NFPP-Si<sub>0.1</sub> at −10&nbsp;°C and 5&nbsp;C rate. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0076" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0076_R_d9736424e3515" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 76 - ACS Nano">76</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2024, American Chemical Society.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Recently, Xin<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0074" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0074_R_d9736424e3523" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 74 - Chem. Eng. J.">74</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> et&nbsp;al. doped cobalt and manganese elements by solid-state reaction to obtain higher voltage NFPP, and obtained Na<sub>4</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub> (NCMFPP). It was found that NCMFPP can provide an initial discharge capacity of up to 139 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;C (1&nbsp;C = 129&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), has an excellent rate performance (up to 75 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 10&nbsp;C), and maintains a capacity retention of 65.2% after 2000 cycles at 10&nbsp;C.</p>
            
            <p>In addition to the substitution of iron sites, anionic groups can also be doped to obtain a more stable structure. Liu<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0075" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0075_R_d9736424e3555" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 75 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">75</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> et&nbsp;al. replaced the PO<sub>4</sub><sup>3−</sup>groups in some sites with SiO<sub>4</sub><sup>4−</sup>groups, and the total density of states analysis showed that the density of states of spin-up and spin-down electrons of NFPP-Si<sub>0.05</sub> were 1.426 and 0.6&nbsp;eV, respectively, which were significantly &lt;3.721 and 3.62&nbsp;eV of pristine NFPP, so the doping of SiO<sub>4</sub><sup>4−</sup> can well reduce the band gap and improve the conductivity. The sodium ion diffusion rates of NFPP-Si0.05 and NFPP were obtained through the Randles-Sevcik equation as 2.1152&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−6</sup> and 6.777&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−7</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The increase in ion diffusion rate did not affect the cycling stability of the materials, with a capacity of 119.4 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;C, and a capacity retention of 84.2% at 5000 cycles at 50&nbsp;C. Cycling tests were further performed at 5&nbsp;C and 10&nbsp;C at a high temperature of 60&nbsp;°C, respectively. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0010">10c,d</a>, the capacity of NFPP-Si<sub>0.05</sub> was higher than that of NFPP at high temperatures and the capacity loss was smaller after 1000 cycles. The cycling test of NFPP-Si<sub>0.1</sub> was additionally conducted at −10&nbsp;°C by Geet&nbsp;al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0076" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0076_R_d9736424e3591" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 76 - ACS Nano">76</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It was revealed that the doped samples have better electrochemical performance at low temperatures. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0010">10e</a>, the NFPP-Si<sub>0.1</sub> still achieves an impressive capacity of 81.2 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles at a rate of 5&nbsp;C, with a capacity retention of 93.6% and a capacity decay rate of 0.0064% per cycle.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202411280-sec-0100">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202411280-sec-0100-title">4 Comparison of Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>4</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>(P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>)</h2>
         
         <p><b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202411280-fig-0011">11</a> compares the merits of Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and NFPP from various aspects, and also with a LIBs polyanionic cathode, LiFePO<sub>4</sub>. It is seen that the most obvious advantage of SIBs cathodes is their rich sodium resources and wide distribution, so as to the corresponding cost. Meanwhile, the energy density, stability and ionic conductivity of LFP superior those of SIB cathodes, originating from intrinsic properties and intensive investigations of LIBs. The environmental impacts of the three are in parallel. To achieve the commercialization of SIBs, the development of low-cost material systems is particularly significant. Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and NFPP are both very promising cathode materials for SIBs, but these two types have their strengths and weaknesses in terms of the material cost, synthesis, operating voltage, suitable application field, etc. <b>Table</b> <a class="tableLink scrollableLink" title="Link to table" href="#adfm202411280-tbl-0003">3</a> gives the physical, chemical, and electrochemical performance of each.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202411280-fig-0011"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/23199c19-7a21-4887-9117-306b25aa1abc/adfm202411280-fig-0011-m.jpg"><picture>

         </section>

            <div class="article-section__table-source"></div>
         </div>
         
         <p>Among SIBs cathodes, the Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> has an average working voltage of 3.8&nbsp;V (vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) and a theoretical specific capacity of 120 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. In experiments, a capacity of over 100 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> has been reported.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0030_R_d9736424e4098" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - J. Energy Chem.">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In comparison, the NFPP has an average working voltage of 3.2&nbsp;V (vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) and a theoretical specific capacity of 129 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The obtained capacity also approaches the theoretical values, for example, 111.7 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.05&nbsp;C.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202411280-bib-0067" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202411280-bib-0067_R_d9736424e4110" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - J. Power Sources">67</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The theoretical energy density of the former is 456&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> and that of the latter is 412.8&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>. Therefore, the difference in the theoretical energy densities of the two is not significant, with Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> being slightly higher than NFPP.</p>
         
         <p>Chemically, the formula of both materials are adjustable. Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> is more stable in the sodium-rich phase, resulting in the production of compounds with non-stoichiometric ratios (Na:Fe &gt; 1:1). Usually, the extra Na occupy Fe crystallographic sites and originally partial occupied Na sites so the chemical formula can be written as Na<sub>2+2x</sub>Fe<sub>2-x</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>. Whereas for NFPP, most reports are in stoichiometry and in a few cases Fe-vacancy was formed without the change of Na content, such as Na<sub>4</sub>Fe<sub>2.91</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>(P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>). The derivation from the ideal chemical formula both causes a small decrease of the theoretical capacity.</p>
         
         <p>In terms of cost, different synthesis methods require different raw materials, heating processes, storage conditions, etc. To simplify the comparison, we first evaluate the basic raw material costs of two types of cathode materials. Taking the price of AR chemicals from Shanghai Macklin Biochemical Technology Co. for example, the synthesis of 1&nbsp;mol Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (assuming a conversion rate of 100%) from Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub>:FeSO<sub>4</sub>·7H<sub>2</sub>O = 1:2 (molar ratio) shall cost ≈140 RMB&nbsp;Wh<sup>−1</sup>, while the synthesis of 1&nbsp;mol NFPP (assuming a conversion rate of 100%) from Fe(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·9H<sub>2</sub>O:CH<sub>3</sub>COONa:NH<sub>4</sub>H<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub> = 3:3:4 (molar ratio) shall cost ≈340 RMB&nbsp;Wh<sup>−1</sup>. The scale-up price shall be a hundred times lower considering the abundance of components. It should be remembered that both materials share a similar synthesis procedure, but the former needs a lower sintering temperature than the latter (350&nbsp;°C vs 550&nbsp;°C). Nevertheless, the Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> is more sensitive to humid exposure and therefore requires a stricter storage condition. In a rough estimation, the cost of preparing Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> shall be lower than that of NFPP.</p>
         
         <p>Another point that needs our attention is the environmental effect, especially the waste during the preparation of the cathode materials. Following the developed methods, the preparation of Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> shall release harmless water and recyclable solvents in the case of the liquid-phase method. As for NFPP, the sintering reaction shall release CO<sub>2</sub>, NO<sub>x</sub>, NH<sub>3</sub>, etc., which shall be harmful to the environment and therefore need extra tail gas treatment. Although the thermal stability of Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> is inferior to NFPP, both are stable under the common application circumstances.</p>
         
         <p>From the viewpoint of a larger context, the energy density of SIBs with either cathode material is three to four times higher than that of conventional lead-acid batteries, and the life span is ten times longer. At the same time, SIBs based on either material are several times cheaper than LIBs in raw material costs, with a slight performance disadvantage (the theoretical energy density of LiFePO<sub>4</sub> is 578&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>). Therefore, both have considerable application prospects where the cost weighs more than energy density such as residential energy storage systems, 5G communication base stations, etc. It shall also be noted that their way to commercialization still faces problems such as low electronic conductivity, limited air stability, volume deformation, scale-up fabrication, etc., which need to be further studied in conjunction with process optimization and theoretical analysis. Demonstration in real batteries with large mass loading, and the long-term stability, safety as well as failure mechanism shall also be illustrated for further development of both materials.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202411280-sec-0110">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202411280-sec-0110-title">5 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>With the global consensus of “one earth, one home”, the replacement of conventional fossil fuel-based chemical energy by green energy sources, such as solar and wind, has become a major trend. In recent years, there has been an increasing interest in sodium-ion batteries to stably store and release such green energy. Two polyanionic compounds, Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>4</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>(P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>), which are potential cathode materials, have become a hot topic of research due to their cheapness and good electrochemical performance. Meanwhile, the low intrinsic conductivity of the polyanionic compounds, coupled with deficiencies such as high resistance to electrons and impurities in the bulk phase due to improper preparation methods, etc., limits the actual specific capacity, rate performance, and stability of the materials. Strategies such as cell structural modulation and carbon composite have been employed to achieve the enhancement of electron and ion transfer capabilities from the microscopic scale and mesoscopic scale, respectively, and indeed have improved the comprehensive performance of the materials. The assembled full batteries based on either cathode have exhibited considerable energy densities and cyclability.</p>
         
         <p>Given the current situation of iron-based polyanionic compounds, the main directions for their future development are summarized as follows. First, the air stability of Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>(SO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> still needs further improvement for easy storage, transport, and treatment. Second, compatible electrolyte systems are urgently needed, where the investigation of the CEI formation mechanism may be crucial for electrolyte design. Third, the research of the full battery should be further increased, and the failure mechanism of the long-cycle battery should be studied in depth from the micro to macro scale. The development in these aspects shall pave the way for practical applications of cost-effective sodium-ion batteries.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
